<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mental-health-manual-revision-papers">Mental Health Manual - revision papers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-health-manual-revision-papers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<p>MODULE 20: MENTAL HEALTH</p>
<p>Code: MEH 408
Hours: 80
Credit: 8</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="module-competence">Module Competence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-competence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This module is designed to enable the learner identify mental health problems and initiate prevention programmes at community level.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="module-outcome">Module Outcome<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-outcome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>By the end of the module, the learner should;</p>
<ol>
<li>Explain the concepts of mental health.</li>
<li>Explain mental disorders.</li>
<li>Incorporate mental health primary health care activities.</li>
<li>Mobilize community resources to provide and coordinate mental health programs.</li>
<li>Explain the myths and misconceptions about mental disorders.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="module-units">Module Units<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-units" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-1-introduction-to-concepts-in-mental-health">UNIT 1: INTRODUCTION TO CONCEPTS IN MENTAL HEALTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-1-introduction-to-concepts-in-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-mental-health">What is Mental Health?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a state of well-being in which the individual realizes his/her potentials/abilities, can cope with normal stresses of life, can work productively and fruitfully and is able to make a contribution to his/her community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="promotion-of-good-mental-health">Promotion of good Mental Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#promotion-of-good-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mental health promotion should be availed to individuals, families, communities and the society. This will be achieved through Primary Health Care spearheaded by primary health care team at the district level in close collaboration with other government sectors, NGO’s, CBO’s, FBO’s and private sector.</p>
<p>Good mental health of individuals, families the communities and the society contribute enormously towards investment and development of social capital which is the most important determinant of our health. This endeavor of promotion of good mental health should be encouraged throughout the human development life cycle, right from pregnancy to old age. This will enable the nation to realize its goals and objectives of the Kenya vision 2030.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-mental-disorders-and-substance-abuse-and-substance-dependence">Prevention of mental disorders and substance abuse and substance dependence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-mental-disorders-and-substance-abuse-and-substance-dependence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is evident that the problem of substance abuse and dependence is on the increase especially amongst the youth. This is largely due to the inability to effectively deal with stress. There is need therefore to increase the knowledge, skills and change of attitude in order to deal with the psychological consequences of stress among vulnerable groups.</p>
<p>In order to be effective in the prevention of mental disorders, substance abuse and substance dependence, it is imperative that close inter-sectoral collaboration needs to be developed amongst sectors and partners.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-mental-disorders-substance-abuse-and-substance-dependence">Treatment of mental disorders, substance abuse and substance dependence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-mental-disorders-substance-abuse-and-substance-dependence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In line with Kenya’s Health Police Framework and Health Sector Reforms, it is envisaged that health services delivery system will be decentralized and integrated throughout the health care delivery system. Therefore, mental health services are no exception. Therefore, treatment of mental disorders and substance abuse and substance dependence will be decentralized and integrated up to the community level. This is possible because all hospitals</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>are gazetted to be mental hospitals for admission and treatment of people suffering from mental disorders in accordance with Sec. 9 of sub-section 2 of the Mental Health Act 1989; Cap 248 of the Laws of Kenya. Mental health services should be provided at different levels of care.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-burden-of-mental-illness">The Burden of Mental illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-burden-of-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There is a report that 450 million people alive today suffer from mental disorders and psychosocial problems such as alcohol and substance dependence and the majority of them suffer silently. One person in every four will be affected by a mental disorder at some stage of life. Major depression is the leading cause of disability and ranks fourth in the ten leading causes of the global burden of disease and is projected to be ranked second within the next 20 years. At least 10 million people attempt suicide every year and one million of them including many who are very young do kill themselves.</p>
<p>The World Health Report 2003 by WHO states that mental, neurological and substance abuse disorders is a major contributor of the overall Global Burden of Disease (GBD). Globally, 13% of overall disability – adjusted life years (DALYs) and 33% of overall years lived with disability (YLDs) are attributable to mental disorders. A large proportion of individuals do not receive any health care for their condition because the mental health infrastructure and services in most countries are grossly insufficient and very insufficient funding and implementation of programs largely due to prevalent stigma and discrimination of patients requiring the services.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rehabilitation-of-mentally-sick-persons-and-substance-dependent-persons">Rehabilitation of mentally sick persons and substance dependent persons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rehabilitation-of-mentally-sick-persons-and-substance-dependent-persons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The psychosocial, occupational and behavioral rehabilitation will be offered at primary, secondary and tertiary levels. However, there would be need for continuing rehabilitation to the family and every community should be encouraged to establish recreational and therapeutic facilities with a view to socially integrates the person to the family and the society at large.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="brief-history-of-mental-health">Brief History of Mental health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#brief-history-of-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Primitive beliefs regarding mental disturbances took several views. Some people thought that an individual with mental illness had been dispossessed of his or her soul and that the only way to wellness would be achieved was if the soul returned.</p>
<p>Others believed that evil spirits or supernatural or magical powers had entered the body. The "care" for these individuals involved a ritualistic exorcism to purge the body of these unwanted forces. This reason consisted of brutal beatings; starvation, or other torturous means.</p>
<p>Still others considered that the mentally ill individuals may have broken a taboo or sinned against another individual or God, for which ritualistic purification was required or various types of retribution were demanded. The correlation of mental illness to demonology or witchcraft led to some mentally ill individuals being burned at the stake.</p>
<p>The position of these ancient beliefs evolved with increasing knowledge about mental illness, as well as changes in cultural, religious, and socio-political attitudes. The work of Hippocrates, about 400 BC, began the movement away from belief in the supernatural powers. Hippocrates associated insanity and mental illness with an irregularity in the interaction of the four (4) body fluids in describing about personalities in psychology.</p>
<p>Disequilibrium among these four humors was thought to cause mental illness and it was often treated by inducing vomiting and diarrhea with potent cathartic drugs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-middle-ages">The Middle Ages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-middle-ages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>During the Middle Ages- AD 500 to 1500, the association of mental illness with witchcraft and supernatural phenomena continued to prevail in the European community. During this period, many severely mentally ill people were sent out to the sea on sailing boats with little guidance and in search of their lost rationality. This operation is credited with engendering the expression "Ship of Fools".</p>
<p>In the same period, in the Middle East- Islamic countries, however, a change in attitude began to occur, from one of mental illness as a result of witchcraft or supernatural to the idea that these individuals were actually ill. This notion give rise to the establishment of "Special Units" for the mentally ill within the general hospitals, as well as institutions specifically designed to house the insane. They can likely be considered the first Asylums for the mentally ill.</p>
<p>Colonial Americans tended to reflect the attitudes of the European community from which they had immigrated. Particularly in the New England area, individuals were punished for behavior attributed to witchcraft. In the 16th and 17th centuries, institutions for the mentally</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>ill were not available in America and care of these individuals became a family responsibility. Those without a family or other resources became the responsibility of the communities in which they lived and were incarcerated in places where they could do no harm to themselves or others.</p>
<p>The first hospital in America to admit mentally ill patients was established in Philadelphia in the middle of the 18th century. Benjamin Rush, often called the father of American Psychiatry, was a physician at the hospital. He initiated the provision of humanistic treatment and care of the mentally ill. Although he included kindness, exercise and socialization, he also employed hasher methods such as blood-letting; purging, various types of physical restraints and extremes of temperatures, reflecting the medical therapies of that era.</p>
<p>The 19th century brought the establishment of a system of state asylums, largely the result of the work of Dorothea Dix, a former New England school teacher, who lobbied tirelessly on behalf of the mentally ill population. She was unfaltering in her belief that mental illness was curable and that state hospitals should provide humanistic therapeutic care. This system of hospital care for the mentally ill grew, but the mentally ill population grew faster. The institution became over-crowded and under-staffed and conditions deteriorated. The therapeutic care reverted to "custodian care". These state hospitals provided the largest resources for the mentally ill until the initiation of the community health movement of the 1960's.</p>
<p>In 1949, the colonial parliament enacted a law, "the Mental Treatment Act", based on a prototype borrowed from Britain. In 1959, the "Mental Treatment Act" was replaced with a more humane Mental health Act, which placed emphasis on community mental health services, repeating the spirit of the new Act in Britain.</p>
<p>The current Mental Health Act became operational in 1959, and for the first time provides for the voluntary treatment of people with mental illness. It also created a regulatory body to oversee its implementation.</p>
<p>As a result of the 1989 Mental Health Act, over half of all government general hospitals opened their doors for psychiatric patients.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="concepts-of-mental-health">Concepts of Mental Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concepts-of-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mental health does not mean absence of mental illness but a sense of wellbeing felt. Mental health and physical health are interrelated and interdependent. Health</p>

<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definitions">Definitions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Health: “A state of complete physical, mental and social well-being and not merely the absence of disease or infirmity” (WHO 1948).</p>
<p>Mental health: The capacity of an individual to form harmonious relationships with others and to participate in or contribute constructively to changes in the social environment. (WHO)</p>
<p>Mental illness/disorder: “Maladaptive responses to stressors from the internal or external environment, evidenced by thoughts, feelings, and behaviors that are incongruent with the local and cultural norms, and interfere with the individual’s social, occupational, and/or physical functioning” (Townsend, 2009).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="consequences-of-mental-illnesses">Consequences of Mental illnesses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#consequences-of-mental-illnesses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Poverty</li>
<li>Poor/inhumane living conditions</li>
<li>Human rights violation</li>
<li>Marginalization &amp; vulnerability</li>
<li>Higher rates of mortality &amp; disability</li>
<li>Physical abuse</li>
<li>Sexual abuse</li>
<li>Neglect</li>
<li>Loss of civil and political rights</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="determinants-of-mental-health">Determinants of Mental Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#determinants-of-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-a-mentally-ill-person">Characteristics of a Mentally ill person<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-mentally-ill-person" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aetiological-factors-of-mental-illnesses">Aetiological factors of Mental Illnesses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiological-factors-of-mental-illnesses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The causes of mental illness can be classified into three broad categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Predisposing factors</li>
<li>Precipitating factors</li>
<li>Perpetuating factors</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Determines the likelihood of one getting a mental illness. Usually, they are adverse experiences one undergoes in early life.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="precipitating-factors">Precipitating Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precipitating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Events that take place shortly before the onset of a disorder. E.g., drug abuse, loss of a job.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="perpetuating-factors">Perpetuating Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#perpetuating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once the disorder has been triggered, these factors do prolong the course of the disease. They may appear long after the original predisposing factors have been treated. Examples include secondary demoralization and withdrawal from social activities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biological-factors">Biological factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biological-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Genetic factors: inheritance of faulty genes and chromosomal abnormalities e.g., down syndrome, Alzheimer's disease.</li>
<li>Physical illness leading to loss of mental capacity e.g., acute malaria</li>
<li>Emotional factors: anxiety and neurotic personality traits cause people to develop psychosomatic disorder Infection, Disease and Toxins</li>
</ul>

<p>&gt; Brain defects or injury: Defects in or injury to certain areas of the brain have also been linked to some mental illnesses.

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="psychological-factors">Psychological Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychological-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Psychological factors that may contribute to mental illness include:</p>
<p>&gt; Severe psychological trauma suffered as a child, such as emotional, physical, or sexual abuse
&gt; An important early loss, such as the loss of a parent
&gt; Neglect
&gt; Poor ability to relate to others</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="socio-cultural-factors">Socio cultural factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#socio-cultural-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Social influence- maladaptive behavior
&gt; Low socio-economic class.
&gt; Social role- a soldier kills then later develops guilty conscious leading to mental illness
&gt; Violence
&gt; Unemployment
&gt; Broken homes</p>
<p>Factors that Influence Attitudes towards Mental Health and Mental Illness in the community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="culture">Culture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#culture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The way people think, behave or feel is shaped by their culture. Culture also determines the features of insanity, for example, who is labelled as insane and under what circumstances.</p>
<p>What is considered insane in one culture may be considered perfectly normal in another. Culture also gives guidelines on the nature of treatment and the identity of the helper.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="education">Education<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The level of education also influences attitudes towards mental health and mental illness.</p>
<p>An educated person has a better understanding of health and mental illness, thus making their attitude more positive.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-beliefs">Health Beliefs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-beliefs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>These will determine whether the individual’s attitude is positive or negative. It will depend on how the patient explains the illness to themselves, that is, whether they believe in germ theory, evil spirits or an imbalance of some kind.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="religion">Religion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#religion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A patient’s reaction to mental illness will often depend on whether or not the patient believes in God or a particular religion, for example, some religions believe that ill health is caused by evil spirits. Usually, religion encourages the followers to be empathetic to sick people.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-0-mental-health-disorders-20-hours">2.0 MENTAL HEALTH DISORDERS 20 HOURS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-0-mental-health-disorders-20-hours" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of the unit learners will be able to:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Differentiate between the two major systems of classifying mental disorders</li>
<li>Classify mental disorders according to each classification system</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-1-classification-of-mental-health-disorders">2.1 classification of mental health disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-1-classification-of-mental-health-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-2-0-anxiety-disorders">2.2.0 Anxiety Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-0-anxiety-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-2-1-introduction">2.2.1 Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-1-introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-2-2-learning-outcomes">2.2.2 Learning Outcomes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-2-learning-outcomes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-2-3-purpose">2.2.3 Purpose<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-3-purpose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The purpose of this unit is to equip the students with knowledge, skills and attitudes to enable them create awareness, identify, demystify and assist in management, effective referral and follow up of anxiety disorders in the community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-2-4-definition-of-anxiety-disorder">2.2.4 Definition of Anxiety Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-4-definition-of-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Anxiety disorders include frequently experiencing intense excessive and persistent worry and fear about everyday situations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-2-5-types-of-anxiety-disorders">2.2.5 Types of anxiety disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-5-types-of-anxiety-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Four types of anxiety disorders include:</p>
<p>a. Generalized anxiety disorder
b. Phobic disorders
c. Obsessive-compulsive disorder (OCD), and
d. Post-traumatic stress disorder (PTSD).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="generalized-anxiety-disorder">Generalized Anxiety Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#generalized-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Generalized Anxiety Disorder is severe ongoing worry that interferes with daily activities. It is characterized by persistent and excessive worry about a number of things like anticipated disaster, concern about money, health, family and work. It is difficult to control the worry.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>It is possible to develop generalized anxiety disorder as a child or an adult. It has symptoms that are similar to panic disorder, obsessive-compulsive disorder and other types of anxiety, but they are all different conditions.</p>
<p>Living with generalized anxiety disorder can be a long-term challenge. In many cases, it occurs along with other anxiety or mood disorders. In most cases, generalized anxiety disorder improves with psychotherapy or medication. Making lifestyle changes, learning coping skills and using relaxation techniques also can help.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-of-generalized-anxiety-disorder">Symptoms of Generalized Anxiety Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-of-generalized-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Generalized anxiety disorder symptoms can vary. They may include:</p>
<p>i. Persistent worrying or anxiety about a number of areas that are out of proportion to the impact of the events.
ii. Overthinking plans and solutions to all possible worst-case outcomes
iii. Perceiving situations and events as threatening, even when they are not.
iv. Difficulty handling uncertainty.
v. Indecisiveness and fear of making the wrong decision.
vi. Inability to set aside or let go of a worry
vii. Inability to relax, feeling restless, and feeling keyed up or on edge
viii. Difficulty concentrating, or the feeling that your mind "goes blank"</p>
<p>Physical signs and symptoms may include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Trouble sleeping</li>
<li>Muscle tension or muscle aches</li>
<li>Trembling, feeling twitchy</li>
<li>Nervousness or being easily startled</li>
<li>Sweating</li>
<li>Nausea, diarrhea or irritable bowel syndrome</li>
<li>Irritability</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="note">Note:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#note" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There may be times when your worries do not completely consume you, but you still feel anxious even when there is no apparent reason. For example, you may feel intense worry about your safety or that of your loved ones, or you may have a general sense that something bad is about to happen.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Your anxiety, worry or physical symptoms cause you significant distress in social, work or other areas of your life. Worries can shift from one concern to another and may change with time and age.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-of-anxiety-disorder-in-children-and-teenagers">Symptoms of Anxiety Disorder in children and teenagers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-of-anxiety-disorder-in-children-and-teenagers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Children and teenagers may have similar worries to adults, but also may have excessive worries about:</p>
<ul>
<li>Performance at school or sporting events</li>
<li>Family members' safety</li>
<li>Being on time (punctuality)</li>
<li>Earthquakes, nuclear war or other catastrophic events</li>
</ul>
<p>A child or teen with excessive worry may:</p>
<ul>
<li>Feel overly anxious to fit in</li>
<li>Be a perfectionist</li>
<li>Redo tasks because they aren't perfect the first time</li>
<li>Spend excessive time doing homework</li>
<li>Lack confidence</li>
<li>Strive for approval</li>
<li>Require a lot of reassurance about performance</li>
<li>Have frequent stomachaches or other physical complaints</li>
<li>Avoid going to school or avoid social situations</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="note">Note:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#note" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some anxiety is normal but one should seek medical attention when:</p>
<ul>
<li>One feel like worrying too much, and it's interfering with work, relationships or other parts of life</li>
<li>One feel like depressed or irritable, have trouble with drinking or drugs, or have other mental health concerns along with anxiety</li>
<li>One feels like have suicidal thoughts or behaviors — seek treatment immediately</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-2-6-causes-of-anxiety-disorder">2.2.6 Causes of Anxiety Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-6-causes-of-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As with many mental health conditions, the cause of generalized anxiety disorder likely arises from a complex interaction of biological and environmental factors, which may include:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Differences in brain chemistry and function</li>
<li>Genetics</li>
<li>Differences in the way threats are perceived</li>
<li>Development and personality</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-2-7-risk-factors-to-anxiety-disorder">2.2.7 Risk factors to Anxiety Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-7-risk-factors-to-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following factors may increase the risk of developing generalized anxiety disorder:</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Personality</strong> - A person whose temperament is timid or negative or who avoids anything dangerous may be more prone to generalized anxiety disorder than others are.</li>
<li><strong>Genetics</strong> - Generalized anxiety disorder may run in families.</li>
<li><strong>Experiences</strong>. People with generalized anxiety disorder may have a history of significant life changes, traumatic or negative experiences during childhood, or a recent traumatic or negative event. Chronic medical illnesses or other mental health disorders may increase risk.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-anxiety-disorder">Complications of Anxiety Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Having generalized anxiety disorder can be disabling. It can:</p>
<ul>
<li>Impair your ability to perform tasks quickly and efficiently because you have trouble concentrating</li>
<li>Take your time and focus from other activities</li>
<li>Sap your energy</li>
<li>Increase your risk of depression</li>
</ul>
<p>Generalized anxiety disorder can also lead to or worsen other physical health conditions, such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Digestive or bowel problems, such as irritable bowel syndrome or ulcers</li>
<li>Headaches and migraines</li>
<li>Chronic pain and illness</li>
<li>Sleep problems and insomnia</li>
<li>Heart-health issues</li>
</ul>
<p>Generalized anxiety disorder often occurs along with other mental health problems, which can make diagnosis and treatment more challenging</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>2.2.8 Prevention of Anxiety Disorder</p>
<p>There is no way to predict what will cause someone to develop generalized anxiety disorder, but you can take steps to reduce the impact of symptoms if you experience anxiety:</p>
<ol>
<li>Get help early. Anxiety, like many other mental health conditions, can be harder to treat if you wait.</li>
<li>Keep a journal. Keeping track of your personal life can help you and your mental health professional identify what's causing you stress and what seems to help you feel better.</li>
<li>Prioritize issues in your life. You can reduce anxiety by carefully managing your time and energy.</li>
<li>Avoid unhealthy substance use. Alcohol and drug use and even nicotine or caffeine use can cause or worsen anxiety. If you are addicted to any of these substances, quitting can make you anxious. If you cannot quit on your own, see your doctor, find a treatment program, or support group to help you</li>
</ol>
<p>2.3.0 Cerebral palsy</p>
<p>Cerebral Palsy is a neurological disorder that refers to a group of non-progressive disorders affecting movement, balance and posture. The condition stems from something anomalous happening to the developing brain or from brain damage before birth, during birth or within the first three years of life (and that is why it is called Infantile).</p>
<p>In Cerebral Palsy, signals from the brain to the body are lost or redirected, resulting in difficulties for people with Cerebral Palsy.</p>
<p>2.3.1 Types of Cerebral Palsy</p>
<p>Cerebral Palsy manifests itself in a variety of ways. The three main types of Cerebral Palsy are:</p>
<p>a. Spastic Cerebral Palsy (the most common, characterized by muscular stiffness in at least one limb),
b. Atetoid Cerebral Palsy (characterized by involuntary movement) and
c. Ataxic Cerebral Palsy (Characterized by difficulties in coordinated movement).</p>
<p>However, the limits between one classification and the other are not so clear and there may be mixed forms of Infantile Cerebral Palsy, or other categorization.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cerebral-palsy-severity-levels">Cerebral Palsy Severity Levels<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebral-palsy-severity-levels" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Cerebral Palsy has a wide range of severity. Some people with Cerebral Palsy may not be blatantly disabled or may seem slightly untidy while others have very limited control of their bodily movements and may have other neurological symptoms, such as eyesight and hearing problems, convulsions, intellectual disability or difficulty in speaking.</p>
<p>Depending On the severity of their condition and their needs, people with Cerebral Palsy can use guardians, sticks, crutches, ambulators or wheelchairs to move, but not all need assistive mobility devices. A bit as happens to all human beings, some have blond hair, other brown or black, others even red: it pays attention to enhance and not discriminate the various differences.</p>
<p>Table 2: Severity Levels of Cerebral Palsy</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Mild Cerebral Palsy</th><th>Moderate – Moderate Cerebral Palsy</th><th>Severe</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>- A person with <strong>mild CP</strong> might walk a little awkwardly, but might not need any special help. <strong>CP</strong> does not get worse over time, though the exact <strong>symptoms</strong> can change over a person's lifetime. All people with <strong>CP</strong> have problems with movement and posture.</td><td>Means a child will need braces, medications, and adaptive technology to accomplish daily activities.</td><td>Severe Cerebral Palsy means a child will require a wheelchair and will have significant challenges in accomplishing daily activities.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="various-therapies-in-the-management-of-cerebral-palsy">VARIOUS THERAPIES IN THE MANAGEMENT OF CEREBRAL PALSY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#various-therapies-in-the-management-of-cerebral-palsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Many people with cerebral palsy undergo:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tendon elongations and other orthopedic procedures, such as serial casting, useful in order to maintain the movement of the limbs.</li>
<li>Others also develop co-morbidity, such as epilepsy and for this reason; they always carry life-saving drugs.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>

<ul>
<li>To improve daily life activities, those living with cerebral palsy can attend weekly physiotherapy and occupational therapy sessions, to better develop motor skills and increase independence.</li>
<li>Speech therapy sessions to improve communication skills and language.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="many-children-with-cerebral-palsy-experience-physical-pain">Many children with Cerebral Palsy experience physical pain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#many-children-with-cerebral-palsy-experience-physical-pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Cerebral Palsy can cause progressive muscle wear, particularly over time. The pain in children living with this disability for several years can result from abnormal movements of the muscles, typical of Cerebral Palsy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="people-with-cerebral-palsy-can-be-independent">People with Cerebral Palsy can be independent<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#people-with-cerebral-palsy-can-be-independent" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>From a young age, many people with Cerebral Palsy learn adaptive skills to maximize their adult independence. Although some people with Cerebral Palsy require high levels of assistance, many others can drive or move independently, live in an independent way and sustain themselves economically.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-4-0-autism">2.4.0 Autism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-4-0-autism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A spectrum of neuropsychiatric disorders characterized by deficits in social interaction and communication, and unusual and repetitive behavior. Some, but not all, people with autism are non-verbal. Autistic disorder is characterized by a withdrawal of the child into the self and into a fantasy world of his or her own creation.</p>
<p>The child has markedly abnormal or impaired development in social interaction and communication.</p>
<p>Activities and interests are restricted and may be considered somewhat bizarre.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="etiology">Etiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-neurological-implications">1. Neurological Implications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-neurological-implications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Autism thought to be caused by abnormalities in brain structures or functions.</li>
<li>Abnormalities have been found in the area of the amygdala, which is known to help regulate aspects of social and emotional behavior.</li>
<li>Elevated levels of serotonin have also been found in a number of people with autism.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-perinatal-influences-women-with-asthma-and-allergies-recorded-during-the-second-trimester-had-a-greater-than-two-fold-elevated-risk-of-having-a-child-affected-by-autism">2. Perinatal influences: Women with asthma and allergies recorded during the second trimester had a greater than two-fold elevated risk of having a child affected by autism.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-perinatal-influences-women-with-asthma-and-allergies-recorded-during-the-second-trimester-had-a-greater-than-two-fold-elevated-risk-of-having-a-child-affected-by-autism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-autism">Types of Autism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-autism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are three quite different types of autism spectrum disorders:</p>
<p>i. Autistic disorder/classic autism,
ii. Asperger syndrome and
iii. Pervasive developmental disorder</p>
<p>The most common form of autism spectrum disorder is classic autism</p>

<table><thead><tr><th>Types of Autism Spectrum Disorders</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Classic autism</td><td>Those with this type of spectrum disorder have “significant language delays, social and communication challenges, and unusual behaviors and interests.” These people are usually affected by intellectual disabilities as well. This type is considered the most severe form of autism and also the most common.</td></tr><tr><td>Asperger syndrome</td><td>People with Asperger’s may experience the same symptoms as the other types of autism but milder.</td></tr><tr><td>People with Asperger syndrome have unusual behaviors and interests, in addition to social challenges.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>They usually don’t have problems with language or intellectual disability</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Pervasive developmental disorder</td><td>This type is typically reserved for those who meet some of the criteria for the other two types, but not all of them. Those affected with PDD-experience milder symptoms or fewer symptoms. Quite typically, they only suffer from social and communication challenges.</td></tr><tr><td>These people tend to be the highest-functioning autistic types and simply do not fit into any of the other categories or types of autism spectrum disorders.</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-criteria-for-autism-spectrum-disorder">Diagnostic criteria for Autism Spectrum Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-criteria-for-autism-spectrum-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
