<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-8-8-prevention-of-dementia">2.8.8 Prevention of dementia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-8-8-prevention-of-dementia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Unfortunately, there has not been shown a sure way of preventing dementia. However, there are steps that may be taken to delay the onset of dementia.</p>
<ul>
<li>Keep the mind active. Mentally stimulating activities, such as reading, solving puzzles and playing word games, and memory training might delay the onset of dementia and decrease its effects.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Be physically and socially active. Physical activity and social interaction might delay the onset of dementia and reduce its symptoms. Move more and aim for 150 minutes of exercise a week.</li>
<li>Quit smoking. Some studies have shown that smoking in middle age and beyond may increase one's risk of dementia and blood vessel (vascular) conditions. Quitting smoking might reduce this risk and will improve health.</li>
<li>Manage cardiovascular risk factors. Treat high blood pressure, high cholesterol, diabetes, and overweight and obesity. High blood pressure might lead to a higher risk of some types of dementia.</li>
<li>Treat health conditions. See the doctor for treatment if you experience hearing loss, depression or anxiety.</li>
<li>Maintain a healthy diet. Eating a healthy diet is important for many reasons, a diet — rich in fruits, vegetables, whole grains, might promote health and lower the risk of developing dementia. Consumption of a healthy diet also improves cardiovascular health, which may help lower dementia risk.</li>
<li>Get quality sleep. Practice good sleep hygiene, and talk to the health care provider if snoring loudly or experiencing periods where one stop breathing (sleep apnoea) or gasp during sleep.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-9-psychoses">2.9 Psychoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-psychoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-9-1-definition-of-psychoses">2.9.1 Definition of Psychoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-1-definition-of-psychoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Psychoses is a mental disorder characterized by a disconnection from reality. Psychoses may occur as a result of a psychiatric illness such as schizophrenia. In other instances, it may be caused by a health condition, medication or Substance Use. People who are experiencing psychoses may have either hallucinations or delusions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-9-2-delusions-and-hallucinations">2.9.2 Delusions and hallucinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-2-delusions-and-hallucinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Delusions and hallucinations are two very different symptoms that are both often experienced by people with psychoses. Delusions and hallucinations seem real to the person who is experiencing them.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>2.9.3 Delusions</p>
<p>A delusion is a false belief or impression that is firmly held even though it's contradicted by reality and what is commonly considered true. There are delusions of paranoia, grandiose delusions, and somatic delusions.</p>
<p>People who are experiencing a delusion of paranoia might think that they are being followed when they aren't or that secret messages are being sent to them. Someone with a grandiose delusion will have an exaggerated sense of importance. Somatic delusion is when a person believes they have a terminal illness, but in reality, they're healthy.</p>
<p>2.9.4 Hallucinations</p>
<p>A hallucination is a sensory perception in the absence of outside stimuli. That means seeing, hearing, feeling, or smelling something that isn't present. A person who is hallucinating might see things that don't exist or hear people talking when they're alone.</p>
<p>2.9.5 Causes of psychoses</p>
<p>Causes of Psychoses are different, and the exact cause isn't always clear. There are certain illnesses that cause psychoses like:</p>
<ul>
<li>brain diseases such as Parkinson's disease, Huntington's disease, and some chromosomal disorders</li>
<li>brain tumors or cysts</li>
</ul>
<p>Some types of dementia may result in psychoses, such as that caused by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Alzheimer's disease</li>
<li>HIV, syphilis, and other infections that attack the brain</li>
<li>some types of epilepsy</li>
<li>stroke</li>
</ul>
<p>2.9.5 Triggers of psychoses</p>
<p>There are also triggers like Substance Use, and other environmental factors. In addition, certain situations can lead to specific types of psychoses developing</p>
<p>2.9.6 Conditions that trigger psychotic episodes</p>
<p>The following conditions have been known to trigger psychotic episodes in some people:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Schizophrenia – A mental health condition that causes hallucinations and delusions</li>
<li>Bipolar disorder – a person with bipolar disorder can have episodes of low mood (depression) and highs or elated mood (mania)</li>
<li>Severe stress or anxiety</li>
<li>Severe depression – feelings of persistent sadness including postnatal depression, which some women experience after having a baby</li>
<li>Lack of sleep</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-9-7-drugs-known-to-trigger-psychotic-episodes">2.9.7 Drugs known to trigger psychotic episodes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-7-drugs-known-to-trigger-psychotic-episodes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following drugs have been known to trigger psychoses:</p>
<ul>
<li>cocaine.</li>
<li>amphetamine (speed)</li>
<li>methamphetamine (crystal meth)</li>
<li>mephedrone (MCAT or miaow)</li>
<li>MDMA (ecstasy)</li>
<li>cannabis.</li>
<li>LSD (acid)</li>
<li>Psilocybins (magic mushrooms)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-9-10-risk-factors-for-developing-psychoses-includes">2.9.10 Risk factors for developing psychoses includes;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-10-risk-factors-for-developing-psychoses-includes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>People are more likely to develop a psychotic disorder if they have a close family member, such as a parent or sibling, who has a psychotic disorder.</li>
<li>Children born with the genetic mutation known as 22q11.2 deletion syndrome are at risk for developing a psychotic disorder, especially schizophrenia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-9-11-types-of-psychoses">2.9.11 Types of psychoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-11-types-of-psychoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-brief-psychotic-disorder">1. Brief psychotic disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-brief-psychotic-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Brief psychotic disorder, sometimes called brief reactive psychoses, can occur during periods of extreme personal stress like the death of a family member. Someone experiencing brief reactive psychoses will generally recover in a few days to a few weeks, depending on the source of the stress.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="drug-or-alcohol-related-psychoses">Drug- or alcohol-related psychoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-or-alcohol-related-psychoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Psychoses can be triggered by the use of alcohol or drugs, including stimulants such as methamphetamine and cocaine. Hallucinogenic drugs like LSD often cause users to see things that aren't really there, but this effect is temporary. Some prescription drugs like steroids and stimulants can also cause symptoms of psychoses. People who have an addition to alcohol or certain drugs can experience psychotic symptoms if they suddenly stop drinking or taking those drugs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organic-psychoses">Organic psychoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organic-psychoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A head injury or an illness or infection that affects the brain can cause symptoms of psychoses. The following are major Psychiatric Disorders that may have psychotic symptoms:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-9-12-bipolar-disorder">2.9.12 Bipolar disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-12-bipolar-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When someone has bipolar disorder, their moods swing from very high to very low. When their mood is high and positive, they may have symptoms of psychoses. They may feel extremely good and believe they have special powers.</p>
<p>When their mood is depressed, the individual may have psychotic symptoms that make them feel angry, sad, or frightened. These symptoms include thinking someone is trying to harm them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-9-13-delusional-disorder">2.9.13 Delusional disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-13-delusional-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A person experiencing delusional disorder strongly believes in things that aren't real.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-9-14-psychotic-depression">2.9.14 Psychotic depression<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-9-14-psychotic-depression" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is major depression with psychotic symptoms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-schizophrenia">2.10 Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Schizophrenia is a lifelong disease that is generally accompanied by psychotic symptoms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-1-diagnosis-of-psychoses">2.10.1 Diagnosis of psychoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-1-diagnosis-of-psychoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Psychoses is diagnosed through a psychiatric evaluation, e.g.; by conducting a Mental status examination. That means a doctor will watch the person's behavior and ask questions about</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>what they're experiencing. Medical tests and X-rays may be used to determine whether there is an underlying illness causing the symptoms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-2-management-of-psychoses">2.10.2 Management of psychoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-2-management-of-psychoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Treating psychoses may involve a combination of medications and therapy. Most people will experience an improvement in their symptoms with treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-3-psychotherapy">2.10.3 Psychotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-3-psychotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-10-3-1-cognitive-behavioral-therapy">2.10.3.1 Cognitive behavioral therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-3-1-cognitive-behavioral-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Psycho-education by explaining what psychoses is to the person and their family. Monitor symptoms of psychoses through means such as keeping a daily log of treatment and behavior.</li>
<li>Cognitive behavioral therapy means meeting regularly to talk with a mental health counselor with the goal of changing thinking and behaviors.</li>
<li>This approach has been shown to be effective in helping people make permanent changes and better manage their illness.</li>
<li>It's often most helpful for psychotic symptoms that don't completely resolve with medications.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-10-3-2-prevent-relapses">2.10.3.2 Prevent Relapses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-3-2-prevent-relapses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Compliance with treatment and appointments</li>
<li>Refer back to health facility if symptoms are observed (even prior to return date).</li>
<li>A person in the psychotic state might not want to seek care, therefore it is important for caregivers to be part of relapse prevention.</li>
<li>Professional to build the trust of the person with psychotic disorders. This might also improve treatment adherence.</li>
<li>Build Relations: It is important for the health</li>
<li>Resume positive social activities, such as hobbies, exercise, social networks, community functions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-10-3-3-community-support">2.10.3.3 Community support<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-3-3-community-support" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Community education and advocacy for integration of persons living with schizophrenia</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>

<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Establish a community treatment support system (treatment buddy for drug adherence)</li>
<li>Community income/ meaningful work support system</li>
<li>Establish a support network to enhance a sense of connection</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-4-prevention-of-psychoses">2.10.4 Prevention of Psychoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-4-prevention-of-psychoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Emphasize on the importance of sufficient rest and sleep</li>
<li>Emphasize on nutritious and diversified diet</li>
<li>Emphasize on some physical activity</li>
<li>Spend time outside</li>
<li>Avoid drugs and alcohol</li>
<li>Referral to seek early treatment</li>
<li>Follow up appointments</li>
<li>Adherence to drug regimen</li>
<li>Encourage support groups</li>
<li>Family support</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-5-alcohol-use-disorders">2.10.5 Alcohol Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-5-alcohol-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are conditions resulting from different patterns of alcohol consumption including acute alcohol intoxication, harmful alcohol use, the alcohol dependence syndrome, and the alcohol withdrawal state.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-6-terms-associated-with-alcohol-use">2.10.6 Terms Associated with Alcohol use;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-6-terms-associated-with-alcohol-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Acute intoxication</strong>: a transient condition following intake of alcohol resulting in disturbances of consciousness, cognition, perception, affect or behaviour.</p>
<p><strong>Harmful use</strong>: a pattern of alcohol consumption that is causing damage to health. The damage may be physical (as in cases of infections related to drug use) or mental (e.g. episodes of depressive disorder) and is often associated with damage to social functioning (e.g. family problems, legal problems or work-related problems).</p>
<p><strong>Alcohol dependence</strong>: a cluster of physiological, behavioral and cognitive phenomena in which the use of alcohol takes on a much higher priority for a given individual than other behaviors that once had greater value.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Alcohol withdrawal state: refers to a group of symptoms that may occur upon cessation/reduction of alcohol after its prolonged daily use. Various factors can impact how drinking alcohol affects your body and behavior.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-6-1-factors-contributing-to-alcohol-use-disorders">2.10.6.1 Factors Contributing to Alcohol Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-6-1-factors-contributing-to-alcohol-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Genetic,
b. Psychological,
c. Social and
d. Environmental factors</p>
<p>Many varied factors are associated with one being involved with alcohol and or drug use. These include the following as shown in figure 1:</p>
<p>Micro-level Environmental Factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Family</li>
<li>School</li>
<li>Peers.</li>
</ul>
<p>Macro-level Environmental Factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Poverty</li>
<li>Social environment</li>
<li>Physical environment.</li>
</ul>

Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>

Figure 4: Factors Associated with Alcoholism</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-6-2-signs-and-symptoms-of-alcohol-use-disorder">2.10.6.2 Signs and Symptoms of Alcohol Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-6-2-signs-and-symptoms-of-alcohol-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Alcohol is taken in larger amounts or over a longer period than was intended.</li>
<li>Persistent desire or unsuccessful efforts to cut down or control alcohol use.</li>
<li>A lot of time is spent in activities necessary to obtain alcohol, use alcohol, or recover from its effects.</li>
<li>Craving, or a strong desire or urge to use alcohol.</li>
<li>Recurrent alcohol use resulting in a failure to fulfil major role obligations at work, school, or home.</li>
<li>Continued alcohol use despite having persistent or recurrent social or interpersonal problems caused or exacerbated by the effects of alcohol.</li>
<li>Important social, occupational, or recreational activities are given up or reduced because of alcohol use.</li>
<li>Recurrent alcohol use in situations in which it is physically hazardous.</li>
<li>Continued use of alcohol despite the knowledge of physical and psychological harm.</li>
<li>A need for markedly increased amounts of alcohol to achieve intoxication or desired effect</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>NOTE: The presence of at least 2 of these symptoms indicates an alcohol use disorder (AUD). The severity of an AUD is graded mild, moderate, or severe:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-6-3-management-of-alcohol-use-disorders">2.10.6.3 Management of Alcohol Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-6-3-management-of-alcohol-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="behavioral-management">Behavioral Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#behavioral-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Behavioral management are aimed at changing drinking behavior through counseling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="medications">Medications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Medications are currently guided by treatment protocols to help people stop or reduce their drinking and prevent relapse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="i-mutual-support-groups">i. Mutual-Support Groups<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-mutual-support-groups" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Alcoholics Anonymous (AA) provide peer support for people quitting or cutting back on their drinking. Combined behavioral and medical management, can lead to better outcomes.</p>
<p><strong>Life course approach to interventions on Alcohol use Prevention</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-10-6-4-preventive-measures-for-alcohol-use-disorders">2.10.6.4 Preventive Measures for Alcohol Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-10-6-4-preventive-measures-for-alcohol-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pregnancy-infancy-and-early-childhood">Pregnancy, Infancy and Early Childhood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pregnancy-infancy-and-early-childhood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These are meant to help mothers understand the causative agents and how exposure to alcohol can impact the general health as well as the growth of the brain of the child. Interventions entail: sensitization on how to protect the unborn child from the effects of alcohol use; Sensitization on how to protect the growing baby from the negative effects of alcohol by engaging both the parents and the community strategies include;</p>
<ul>
<li>targeting pregnant women with alcohol use disorders</li>
<li>Prenatal, Antenatal, Postnatal and infancy visitation Early childhood education</li>
<li>Community-based multi-component</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="middle-childhood">Middle Childhood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#middle-childhood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>

<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>These include interventions to help parents learn new skills on parenting to help them be able to bring up kids who are not predisposed to alcoholism. Examples are skills on how to handle pressure, disciplining the child, positive stress coping mechanisms, positive environment for the growing child etc. The interventions include;</p>
<ul>
<li>Parenting skills programmes</li>
<li>Personal and social/life skills education</li>
<li>Community based -multi-component (community stakeholder involvement)</li>
<li>Classroom environment improvement programmes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-adolescence">Early Adolescence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-adolescence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are interventions targeting parents and the community on how to handle adolescents who are beginning to develop abstract thinking and curiosity. Interventions include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Parenting skills programmes</li>
<li>Prevention education - based on personal and social skills and social influences</li>
<li>School policy and culture</li>
<li>Addressing individual psychological vulnerabilities</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adolescence">Adolescence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adolescence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are interventions that target adolescents themselves. At this stage, the adolescents can think abstractly and make a judgement based on their own conviction, or peer influence. Therefore, interventions for them include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mentoring</li>
<li>Alcohol and tobacco policies</li>
<li>Community multi-component initiatives (Community stakeholders involvement)</li>
<li>Media Campaigns</li>
<li>Brief Intervention</li>
<li>Behaviour change communication</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="late-adolescence-and-adulthood">Late Adolescence and Adulthood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#late-adolescence-and-adulthood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The interventions target the entire population in a community focusing on key stakeholders (the police, the law makers, the workplace, the various communities, the community influencers/spokesmen, the administrative unit etc.) The interventions include;</p>
<ul>
<li>Prevention education based on personal and social skills and social influences</li>
<li>School policy and culture</li>
<li>Addressing individual psychological vulnerabilities</li>
<li>Alcohol and tobacco policies</li>
<li>Community multi-component initiatives</li>
<li>Media Campaigns</li>
<li>Workplace prevention</li>
<li>Entertainment venues</li>
<li>Brief intervention</li>
<li>Behaviour change communication</li>
<li>Mentorship and coaching</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-11-drug-use-disorders">2.11 Drug Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-11-drug-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-11-1-definition-of-terms-associated-with-drug-use-disorder">2.11.1 Definition of Terms Associated with Drug Use Disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-11-1-definition-of-terms-associated-with-drug-use-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Drug use disorder is a condition resulting from different patterns of drug use, including overdose, intoxication, harmful or hazardous drug use.</p>
<p>Due to their psychoactive and dependence-producing properties, psychoactive substances have the potential to harm individuals' health and lead to societal harm. The nature and severity of the harm relate to many factors, including the properties of the psychoactive substance itself, the form and mode of administration used, the characteristics of the person taking the substance, and the social context in which it is taken.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="terms-associated-with-drug-use-disorders">Terms associated with drug use disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terms-associated-with-drug-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Drug: is any substance other than food that affects the function of the body</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-drug-abuse">2. Drug abuse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-drug-abuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the misuse or overuse of a substance in a way different from the way it is generally used either in medical or social circumstances. The term also refers to the use of any illegal substance including alcohol if one is under-age as well as continued use of a substance even though it is causing problems in one's life.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Acute intoxication: a transient condition following use of drugs resulting in disturbances of consciousness, cognition, perception, affect or behaviour.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Harmful use: a pattern of drug use that is causing damage to health. The damage may be physical (as in cases of infections related to drug use) or mental (e.g. episodes of depressive disorder) and is often associated with damage to social functioning (e.g. family problems, legal problems or work-related problems).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drug dependence: a cluster of physiological, behavioral and cognitive phenomena in which the use of drugs takes on a much higher priority for a given individual than other behaviors that once had greater value.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drug withdrawal state: refers to a group of symptoms that may occur upon cessation/reduction of drugs after prolonged use</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-11-2-causes-of-drug-use-disorders">2.11.2 Causes of Drug Use Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-11-2-causes-of-drug-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Genetic /Hereditary factors
ii. Environmental, noise, extremes of temperatures
iii. Availability of drug
iv. Curiosity
v. Social factors- Adverse life events/ -break ups, divorce, separation, bereavement, displacement
vi. War, conflict &amp; violence
vii. Underlying medical and Psychiatric conditions
viii. Trauma, especially head injury
ix. Peer pressure
x. Sexual malfunction /dysfunction</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-11-3-diagnostic-criteria-for-drug-dependence">2.11.3 Diagnostic Criteria for Drug Dependence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-11-3-diagnostic-criteria-for-drug-dependence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For one to be diagnosed with drug dependency they need to present with the following:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Table 3:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Presentation</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Tolerance</td><td>Need for higher doses to achieve the same effect.</td></tr><tr><td>Withdrawal Symptoms</td><td>Symptoms that develop when an individual who is physically addicted to a drug abstains (intentionally or otherwise) and levels of the chemicals in the body begin to diminish or reduce</td></tr><tr><td>Impaired control</td><td>Persistent desire to use substance, unsuccessful attempts at controlling use, or using for longer period than intended</td></tr><tr><td>Neglecting activities</td><td>Alternative activities are neglected or abandoned due to substance use</td></tr><tr><td>Time spent using drugs</td><td>Much time is devoted to obtaining, using, or recovering from the effects of substance use</td></tr></tbody></table>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-11-5-classification-of-drugs-by-effect">2.11.5 Classification of Drugs by Effect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-11-5-classification-of-drugs-by-effect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Table 5: Drug Effects</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Type of Drug</th><th>Effects</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Depressants</td><td>Depressants are drugs that impair the activity of the central nervous system by enhancing the effects of GABA, a neurotransmitter which inhibits connectivity among neurons.</td></tr><tr><td>DEPRESSANTS: SHORT-TERM EFFECTS</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>|   | • Slow brain function
• Slowed pulse and breathing
• Lowered blood pressure
• Poor concentration
• Confusion
• Fatigue2
• Dizziness
• Slurred speech
• Fever
• Sluggishness
• Visual disturbances
• Dilated pupils
• Disorientation, lack of coordination
• Depression
• Difficulty or inability to urinate
• Addiction</p>
<p>Long-term use of depressants can produce:
• depression,
• chronic fatigue,
• breathing difficulties,
• sexual problems and
• Sleep problems.</p>
<p>As a dependency on the drug increases, cravings, anxiety or panic are common if the user is unable to get more.</p>
<p>Withdrawal symptoms include insomnia, weakness and nausea.</p>
<p>For continual and high-dose users, agitation, high body temperature, delirium, hallucinations and convulsions can occur.</p>
<p>Unlike withdrawal from most drugs, withdrawal from depressants can be life threatening.  |
| --- | --- |
|  Stimulants | Stimulants are a class of drugs, which enhance central nervous system activity and block  |</p>

<p>|   | the re-uptake of the neurotransmitters norepinephrine and dopamine.
The short-term effects of stimulants can include:
• Euphoria
• Accelerated alertness
• Enhanced energy
• Increased arousal
• Rapid heart rate
• Unusual behavior
The extended use of stimulants can cause severe effects on the body such as:
• Tremors
• Tachycardia
• Insomnia
• Tooth decay
• Heart attack
• Brain damage
• Organ damage
• Sudden death  |

|  Hallucinogens | Hallucinogens are mind-altering drugs which cause false perceptions of reality.
The short-term effects of Hallucinogens can include:
• Hallucinations
• Fluctuations in heart rate
• Intense feelings and sensory feedback
• Feelings of distorted time
• Dry mouth
• Anxiety or paranoia
The extended abuse of some Hallucinogens may produce a variety of long-term effects, including:
• Speech problems and memory loss from repeated PCP use
• Bladder ulcers and kidney problems from Ketamine use
• Paranoia  |</p>

• Mental problems

|  Inhalants | Inhalants are volatile substances that produce chemical vapors that can be inhaled to induce a psychoactive, or mind-altering, effect. Although other abused substances can be inhaled, the term "inhalants" is used to describe a variety of substances whose main common characteristic is that they are rarely, if ever, taken by any route other than inhalation.</p>
<p>Some of the more common negative effects of inhalant use include:
• Brain damage
• Liver damage
• Kidney failure
• Respiratory distress
• Blindness
• Intestinal inflammation
• Ulcers
• Hallucinations
• Cardiac arrest
• Loss of sense of smell  |</p>
<p>2.11.6 Management of drug use disorders</p>
<p>Entails multiple approaches that include:</p>
<p>I. <strong>Detoxification</strong>: As one stops taking drugs, allowing the drugs to leave the body. One may need healthcare supervision to detox safely.</p>
<p>II. <strong>Medication-assisted therapies</strong>: During detox, medicine can help control cravings and relieve withdrawal symptoms.</p>
<p>III. <strong>Psychosocial Support</strong>:</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>Behavioral therapies</strong>: Cognitive behavioral therapy or other psychotherapy (talk therapy) can help deal with addiction’s cause. Therapy also helps build self-esteem and teaches healthy coping mechanisms.</p>

<p>2.11.7 Prevention of substance use disorder</p>
<p>The focus in prevention of substance use is to help people, particularly young people,</p>
<ul>
<li>Avoid or delay the initiation of the use of substance use,</li>
<li>If they have already started using substances, link to relevant services to prevent the development of dependency.</li>
<li>School-based awareness programmes for children to impart the messages to them at an early age so that they can make healthy choices in life when they grow up.</li>
<li>Youth groups in the community, who are important role models, may be roped in through awareness programmes and making use of them to in turn to spread the message.</li>
<li>Women self-help groups can be educated as members of such groups may be affected by the family member's drug use and most importantly become co-dependent.</li>
<li>Local politicians/ influencers need to be addressed, as they can support the cause.</li>
<li>Religious heads from the community need to be involved, as they will positively influence the community to seek professional help.</li>
<li>County governments can be periodically approached to give out appropriate public service messages.</li>
<li>Local NGOs working in the community need to be made as the focal point of contact.</li>
</ul>
<p>Awareness needs to be created about the help that is available for the family, educational institution, substance users. This will call for:</p>
<ul>
<li>Creating awareness of the different toll-free numbers for affected individuals or their families or friends to approach.</li>
<li>Disseminate Posters/pamphlets/notices to be displayed.</li>
<li>Seeking help from the media including print, TV and radio (community media)</li>
<li>The community health volunteers should be trained on referral and follow up.</li>
<li>Primary care givers need to be sensitized on substance use disorders prevention</li>
<li>Community dialogue days can be conducted in partnership with appropriate treatment centres and a host organization from the community.</li>
<li>Observing all important days like International day against illicit drugs and trafficking, Anti-tobacco day, etc., helps to increase awareness about the problem of substance abuse and addiction.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Law/police departments need to be engaged to prevent legal problems associated with substance use and intervene for persons with substance use in conflict with the law.</li>
<li>Use of social media is an increasingly powerful tool even in rural areas. This can work in both enhancing awareness on treatment as well as be exploited by substance using networks.</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Prevention of substance use disorders in communities calls for a multi-pronged approach and must address the various stages of the life cycle of the population and various segments of the community.</p>
<p>UNIT 3: DRUGS AND SUBSTANCE ABUSE</p>
<p>DEFINITIONS OF TERMS</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>A substance is considered abused if it is deliberately used to induce physiological or psychological effects or both, for the purposes other than therapeutic ones, and when its use contributes to health risks, the disruption of psychological functioning, adverse social consequences or a combination of them.</p>
<p>A drug can be defined as a substance, which may be chemical, synthetic or natural, which when taken in by a living organism may modify or affect one or more of its functions</p>
<p>Drug misuse is considered to be the misuse of medicine and incorrect use of drugs or medicines with the intention of causing body changes. It can also be said to be taking of medicine/drugs without the doctor's prescription</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="commonly-abused-drugs-and-substances">Commonly Abused Drugs and Substances<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#commonly-abused-drugs-and-substances" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most commonly abused substances are alcohol and tobacco. They are in fact termed as gateway substances to other drugs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="alcohol">Alcohol<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcohol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Alcohol includes wine, spirits, beer, "busaa", "muratina", "mnazi", "changaa" and others such as "kumi kumi" "machozi" etc). Alcohol is considered a depressant which slows and lowers the functions of the brain, e.g. thinking, concentration, and recognition, making decisions and initiating reasoned actions. The effect of alcohol on the brain make people feel relaxed, stop worrying about what other people think of them, and have a good time.</p>
<p>The initial effect of alcohol makes one feel stimulated, become talkative and more active. As some continue taking more alcohol, mood and social behavior changes, some people become depressed and remorseful; others become belligerent (become abusive or violent)</p>
<p>Depressive drunks may slow down, stumble, loudly confess their sins and failures and slur in words. The Amoral drunks may pick up quarrels and fights and other reckless behaviors. When they fall asleep they wake up with a hangover which includes fatigue, headache and nausea. They may also feel restlessness during the day and this can affect their productivity</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tobacco">Tobacco<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tobacco" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Tobacco contains 4,000 different chemicals many of which are harmful. Nicotine, carbon monoxide and tar are the three main chemicals that affect the human body and cause diseases. Tobacco can be smoked, snorted or chewed</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-tobacco">Effects of Tobacco<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-tobacco" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The tar in the cigarette is deposited in the lungs causing lung damage and even lung cancer. Carbon monoxide present in cigarettes also affects the chemical activity of the heart, which encourages deposits on the walls of the arteries leading to blockage that may cause blood circulation problems.</p>
<p>For pregnant women this reduces the amount of oxygen reaching the baby during pregnancy. Smoking can also cause spontaneous abortion and other complications during pregnancy, low birth weight babies and stillbirths as well as prenatal mortality in women</p>
<p>Smoking also leads to increased incidences of severe coughing, sneezing and shortness of breath on exertion. Peptic ulcers in the stomach and duodenum, cancer of the mouth, nose, throat, esophagus, pancreas, bladder, cervix and leukemia are other diseases caused by smoking</p>
<p>Economically, although smoking contributes to a country's revenue, it eats into the family budget. It is also very costly in the treatment of diseases associated with smoking</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cannabis-sativa">Cannabis Sativa<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cannabis-sativa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is also known as Bang, Marijuana (street names -grass, weed, pot, jive, reeter, and ganja. This drug is rolled into cigarette and smoked; and can also be chewed. It can also be processed into more potent form known as hashish.</p>
