<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-drug-and-substance-abuse">EFFECTS OF DRUG AND SUBSTANCE ABUSE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-drug-and-substance-abuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A drug abuser undergoes several stages</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="stage-one-tolerance">Stage one: Tolerance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-one-tolerance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A person starts abusing drugs for the first time and more into habitual use where the drug takes the central stage of his/her life. This repeated use leads to changes in the brain and nervous system so that the user needs more of the drug to get the expected effect</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="stage-two-dependence">Stage Two: Dependence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-two-dependence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The body of the drug abuser demands that he takes more drugs. The abuser is now in the stage of psychic or physical compulsive desire to continually use the drug, either to experience the desired effects or avoid the consequences of withdrawal. The suffering from withdrawal is like an emotional prison trapping the drug abuser.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="stage-three-addiction">Stage Three: Addiction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-three-addiction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The user is now a victim of drugs and cannot help himself or herself. He/she has now developed physical and psychological need for the drug for the body to function normally. This may lead to damage of vital organs in the body such as lungs, liver, central nervous system etc. and the work output may deteriorate</p>
<p>The user lives in denial and has little concern for future life. The use may manipulate other people to get what he/she wants so as to maintain the habit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="relationship-between-substance-abuse-and-hiv-aids">RELATIONSHIP BETWEEN SUBSTANCE ABUSE AND HIV &amp; AIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#relationship-between-substance-abuse-and-hiv-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sharing of needles by substance abusers can lead to HIV infection and AIDS</p>
<p>Substance abusers stand a high risk of spreading HIV &amp;AIDS through sexual intercourse</p>
<p>Substance use is known to impair a person's judgment and for this reason the person may expose himself/herself to the virus</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The uncontrollable properties of psychoactive substances lead to sexual and other highrisk behaviors that individuals might otherwise avoid</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-drug-and-substance-abuse">MANAGEMENT OF DRUG AND SUBSTANCE ABUSE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-drug-and-substance-abuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="detoxification-process">Detoxification Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#detoxification-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is getting the drug out of the person's system and seeing him/her through the withdraw system, where drugs dependency starts</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="counseling">Counseling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#counseling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Characteristics of clients who are motivated to change</p>
<ul>
<li>Accept the diagnosis given</li>
</ul>
<p>Uncomfortable about the behavior</p>
<ul>
<li>Talk about change willingly</li>
<li>Agree with the counselor</li>
</ul>
<p>Follow the course of action</p>
<ul>
<li>They will start, continue and try to sustain change</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: The counselor's role is to motivate the client and affirm any small achievement</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="effective-motivation-strategy">Effective Motivation Strategy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effective-motivation-strategy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Motivation is a state of readiness or eagerness to change, which may fluctuate from one time situation to another. This stage is one that can be influenced. Prochaska &amp; Diclemente developed a wheel of change model that shows the stages through which clients pass in course of changing a problem. These include:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="i-pre-contemplation">i. Pre-contemplation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-pre-contemplation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<ol>
<li>A person is not considering change, has not contemplated having a problem or needing to make a change. People are very defensive here</li>
<li>People seldom present themselves for treatment but they are made under coercion</li>
<li>They need information and feedback to raise awareness about the problem and the possibility of change</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>ii. Contemplation</p>
<ol>
<li>Awareness is already raised but the client considers change and rejects it. They are ambivalent</li>
<li>When they talk about self, they go back and forth between reasons for concern and justification for un concern (caused by pathological personality traits or defense mechanisms)</li>
<li>The counselor task at this stage is to help tip the balance in favor for change</li>
<li>People come for consultation in the contemplation stage. As a counselor practice motivational interviewing</li>
</ol>
<p>iii. Determination Stage</p>
<p>This is a window of opportunity. The counselor helps the client to match i.e. helping client to find a change strategy that is acceptable, accessible, appropriate and effective</p>
<p>iv. Action Stage</p>
<ol>
<li>This is what most people think is therapy</li>
<li>The person engages in particular actions intended to bring about change</li>
<li>These changes may or may not be assisted by formal counseling. the goal during this stage is to produce a change in the area</li>
</ol>
<p>v. Maintenance Stage</p>
<ol>
<li>the challenge is to sustain the change accomplished by previous action to prevent relapse</li>
<li>maintaining change may require a different set of skills and strategies e.g. quitting a drug, reducing drinking or loosing weight is an initial step followed by the challenge of maintaining assistance or moderation</li>
</ol>
<p>vi. Relapse</p>
<p>Help the client to renew the process of contemplation, determination and action stages without becoming stuck or demoralized because of the relapse</p>
<p>Motivational Interviewing</p>
<p>What is motivational interviewing?</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Motivation is defined as a probability that a person will enter into, continue and adhere to specific change strategy. It is the counselor's responsibility not only to dispense advice but also to motivate - to increase likelihood that the client will follow a recommended course of action to change. A counselor is like a salesman and motivation is inherent and central part of the professional task.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-motivation-interviewing">Principles of Motivation Interviewing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-motivation-interviewing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some people need this, once unstuck, no longer immobilized by conflicting motivations, they have the skill and resources they need in order to make a lasting change</p>
<p>Important to people who are reluctant to change and endure ambivalent in changing</p>
<p>For others, motivational interviewing is a prelude to treatment</p>
<p>It creates openness to change which paves way for further therapeutic work Responsibility for change relies on the individual</p>
<p>This does not denote that therapists are powerless or helpless, they exert a lot of influence</p>
<ul>
<li>The strategies are more persuasive than coercive, more supportive than argumentative (the therapist creates a conducive environment for change)</li>
</ul>
<p>The therapist is increasing client's intrinsic motivation, so that change arises from within rather than being imposed from without</p>
<p>Done properly, client presents the argument for change, rather than therapist.</p>
<p>Motivation interviewing employs a variety of strategies especially derived from person centered therapy</p>
<p>Counselor may appear relatively active</p>
<p>But the motivational interviewing proceeds with a strong sense of purpose, clear strategies and skills for pursuing that purpose and a sense of timing to intervene in particular ways at particular moments.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="motivational-interviewing-approach">Motivational Interviewing Approach<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#motivational-interviewing-approach" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t  u  d  o  c  u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Systematically directs the client towards motivation for change. Offers the counselor's own advice and feedback where appropriate. Empathic reflection is used selectively to reinforce certain processes.</p>
<p>Seeks to create and amplify the client's discrepancy in order to enhance motivation for change.</p>
<p>De-emphasis on basis of labels; acceptance of “alcoholism” or other labels seen as unnecessary for change.</p>
<p>Emphasize on personal choice and responsibility for deciding future behavior. Therapists conduct the objective evaluation, but focuses on eliciting the client's own concerns.</p>
<p>Resistance is seen as interpersonal behavior pattern influenced by therapists' behavior.</p>
<p>Resistance is met with reflection.</p>
<p>Treatment goals and change strategies are negotiated between the client and therapist, based on data and acceptability. Client's involvement in the process and acceptance of goals are vital.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-approaches">Treatment Approaches<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-approaches" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Individual approaches</li>
<li>In patient counseling</li>
<li>Participation in AA (Alcohol Anonymous) support groups</li>
<li>Change can be enhanced by Cognitive approaches, Behavioral modification, Person centered Therapy, Solution Focused Brief Therapy</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="re-integration">Re-integration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#re-integration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Counseling dysfunctional families and children - they suffer from shame, anger, distorted thinking</li>
</ul>
<p>The clients need to be appreciated and accepted by the community to help them become productive members of the society.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preventive-measures-to-drug-and-substance-abuse">PREVENTIVE MEASURES TO DRUG AND SUBSTANCE ABUSE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventive-measures-to-drug-and-substance-abuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Proper education on factors that contribute to the problem and deal with them. There is need to educate the public on proper use of legal drugs.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Create awareness in the community, at work place, in schools and places of worship. Educating people about drugs removes ignorance</p>
<p>Media campaigns to highlight negative effects of drug use</p>
<p>Effective parenting helps to raise a drug free child. Functional families nature a normal child.</p>
<p>Occupational therapist to train workers how to cope with stress at work place. Teach life skills and other skills related to their jobs e.g. interpersonal skills, assertiveness etc.</p>
<p>To detect the drug users and, help them through drug counseling, treatment and rehabilitations</p>
<p>Effective government policies on drug trafficking</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="life-skills-necessary-in-the-prevention-of-drug-and-substance-abuse">LIFE SKILLS NECESSARY IN THE PREVENTION OF DRUG AND SUBSTANCE ABUSE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-skills-necessary-in-the-prevention-of-drug-and-substance-abuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Assertiveness</li>
<li>Self-awareness</li>
<li>Self-esteem</li>
<li>Communication</li>
<li>Decision-making</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="values-necessary-in-the-prevention-of-drug-and-substance">VALUES NECESSARY IN THE PREVENTION OF DRUG AND SUBSTANCE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#values-necessary-in-the-prevention-of-drug-and-substance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phobic-disorders">Phobic Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phobic-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition-of-phobia">Definition of Phobia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-phobia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A phobia is an excessive and irrational fear reaction. Persons with phobia may experience a deep sense of dread or panic when they encounter the source of the fear.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="type-of-phobias">Type of Phobias<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#type-of-phobias" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol>
<li>Agoraphobia</li>
</ol>
<p>Agoraphobia is a fear of places or situations that you cannot escape. The word itself refers to “fear of open spaces.” People with agoraphobia fear being in large crowds or trapped outside the home. They often avoid social situations altogether and stay inside their homes.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Social phobia</li>
</ol>
<p>Social phobia is also referred to as social anxiety disorder. It refers to extreme worry about social situations and it can lead to self-isolation. A social phobia can be so severe that the simplest interactions, such as ordering at a restaurant or answering the telephone, can cause panic. People with social phobia often go out of their way to avoid public situations.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Glossophobia</li>
</ol>
<p>This is known as performance anxiety, or the fear of speaking in front of an audience. People with this phobia have severe physical symptoms when they even think about being in front of a group of people. Glossophobia treatments can include either therapy or medication.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Acrophobia:</li>
</ol>
<p>This is the fear of heights. People with this phobia avoid mountains, bridges, or the higher floors of buildings. Symptoms include vertigo, dizziness, sweating, and feeling as if they’ll pass out or lose consciousness.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Claustrophobia</li>
</ol>
<p>This is a fear of enclosed or tight spaces. Severe claustrophobia can be especially disabling if it prevents you from riding in cars or elevators.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Aviophobia:</li>
</ol>
<p>This is also known as the fear of flying.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Dentophobia:</li>
</ol>
<p>Dentophobia is a fear of the dentist or dental procedures. This phobia generally develops after an unpleasant experience at a dentist’s office. It can be harmful if it prevents you from obtaining needed dental care.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>Hemophobia:
This is a phobia of blood or injury. A person with hemophobia may faint when they come in contact with their own blood or another person’s blood.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Arachnophobia: This means fear of spiders.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cynophobia: This is a fear of dogs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ophidiophobia: People with this phobia fear snakes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nyctophobia:
This phobia is a fear of the nighttime or darkness. It almost always begins as a typical childhood fear. When it progresses past adolescence, it is considered a phobia.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Risk factors of Phobic Disorders</p>
<ul>
<li>Genetic and environmental factors can cause phobias. Children who have a close relative with an anxiety disorder are at risk of developing a phobia.</li>
<li>Distressing events, such as nearly drowning, can bring on a phobia.</li>
<li>Exposure to confined spaces, extreme heights, and animal or insect bites can all be sources of phobias.</li>
<li>Age</li>
<li>Socioeconomic status</li>
<li>Gender seem to be risk factors only for certain phobias. For example, women are more likely to have animal phobias.</li>
<li>Children or people with a low socioeconomic status are more likely to have social phobias.</li>
</ul>
<p>Symptoms Associated with Phobias
The most common and disabling symptom of a phobia is a panic attack. Features of a panic attack include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pounding or racing heart</li>
<li>Shortness of breath</li>
<li>Rapid speech or inability to speak</li>
<li>Dry mouth</li>
<li>Upset stomach</li>
<li>Nausea</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Elevated blood pressure</li>
<li>Trembling or shaking</li>
<li>Chest pain or tightness</li>
<li>A choking sensation</li>
<li>Dizziness or lightheadedness</li>
<li>Profuse sweating</li>
<li>A sense of impending doom</li>
</ul>
<p>A person with a phobia does not have to have panic attacks for accurate diagnosis, however.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-phobic-disorders">Management of Phobic Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-phobic-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Treatment for phobias can involve therapeutic techniques, medications, or a combination of both.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-cognitive-behavioral-therapy">1. Cognitive behavioral therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-cognitive-behavioral-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Cognitive behavioral therapy (CBT) is the most commonly used therapeutic treatment for phobias. It involves exposure to the source of the fear in a controlled setting. This treatment can decondition people and reduce anxiety.</p>
<p>The therapy focuses on identifying and changing negative thoughts, dysfunctional beliefs, and negative reactions to the phobic situation. New CBT techniques use virtual reality technology to expose people to the sources of their phobias safely.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-medication">2. Medication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-medication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Antidepressants and anti-anxiety medications can help calm emotional and physical reactions to fear. Often, a combination of medication and professional therapy is the most helpful.</p>
<p>&gt; <strong>NOTE:</strong>
&gt;
&gt; If you have a phobia, it is critical that you seek treatment. Overcoming phobias can be difficult, but there is hope. With the right treatment, you can learn to manage your fears and lead a productive, fulfilling life.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-phobic-disorders">Prevention of Phobic Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-phobic-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are no measures to prevent phobic disorders but the following ways are ways to overcome:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Relaxation – If you face a situation in which fear or panic are beginning to take hold, simple relaxation techniques can help. Relax your muscles and mind by forming images of a place you would rather be. This can release tension and bring you back down.</p>
<p>Face your phobia - avoiding fears only makes them scarier. Whatever your fear, if you face it, it should start to fade</p>
<p>Challenge it intellectually- If you begin to feel panic and anxiety when facing your fear, you need to challenge the thoughts you have about your anxiety</p>
<p>Breathe through panic- If you start to get a faster heartbeat or sweating palms, the best thing is not to fight it. Stay where you are and simply feel the panic without trying to distract yourself. Place the palm of your hand on your stomach and breathe slowly and deeply. The goal is to help the mind get used to coping with panic, which takes the fear of “fear” away.</p>
<p>Talk about it - Sharing fears takes away a lot of their scariness</p>
<p>Utilize the “AWARE” technique of facing panic attacks and allowing it to pass - The steps involved in “AWARE” are “Acknowledge and Accept,” in which you accept the oncoming attack, realize that it’s scary, but also accept that it is not dangerous. Once you have accomplished this, you need to “Wait and Watch.” Here, you’re not trying to run away from the fear, but are instead letting it wash over you. Next are the “Action” steps, in which you bring the panic under control with breathing and resume the fearful activity. Finally, you’ll want to “Repeat” the steps if necessary, and then acknowledge that no matter how it feels now, the attack will come to an “End.”</p>
<p>Play music games- during a panic attack muscles tense up. That’s why its recommended that people practice muscle control by intentionally tightening their muscles for 10 to 15 seconds, and then relaxing them. This gives people a sense of empowerment, that they, and not their emotions, are in charge of their muscles,</p>
<p>Beware of the effects of caffeine- high caffeine intake or caffeine addiction can only heighten your anxiety and increase your reaction to phobias</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-0-myths-and-misconception-about-mental-health">4.0 MYTHS AND MISCONCEPTION ABOUT MENTAL HEALTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-0-myths-and-misconception-about-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-biggest-misconceptions-about-mental-illness">The Biggest Misconceptions About Mental Illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-biggest-misconceptions-about-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mental health has long been misunderstood.</p>
<p>Only until more recently, mental illnesses and mental health disorders were taboo topics. People were uncomfortable talking about these subjects or their mental health struggles. As a result, rumors and misunderstandings about mental illnesses ran wild. The media played no helping hand with exaggerated stories and extreme cases being showcased regularly. Although there has been progress, there are still several popular misconceptions about mental disorders that many people still believed to be true and may even be falsely spreading.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-mental-health-misconceptions-myths">Common Mental Health Misconceptions &amp; Myths<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-mental-health-misconceptions-myths" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Although these common misconceptions about mental illness can seem innocuous, they can be damaging in several ways. These mental health myths continue to perpetuate toxic stereotypes that may keep someone from getting the help they need. Some may fear how others will view them if they come forward and ask for help. Others may avoid treatment because of the rumors about the type of care they will receive. This can leave many people struggling on their own and internalizing these negative views on mental illness that could ultimately make their problems worse.</p>
<p><strong>Myth: Mental health problems don't affect me.</strong></p>
<p><strong>Fact:</strong> Mental health problems are actually very common. In 2020, about:</p>
<ul>
<li>One in five American adults experienced a mental health issue</li>
<li>One in 6 young people experienced a major depressive episode</li>
<li>One in 20 Americans lived with a serious mental illness, such as schizophrenia, bipolar disorder, or major depression</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Myth:</strong> Children don't experience mental health problems.</p>
<p><strong>Fact:</strong> Even very young children may show early warning signs of mental health concerns. These mental health problems are often clinically diagnosable, and can be a product of the interaction of biological, psychological, and social factors.</p>
<p>Half of all mental health disorders show first signs before a person turns 14 years old, and three-quarters of mental health disorders begin before age 24.</p>
<p>Unfortunately, only half of children and adolescents with diagnosable mental health problems receive the treatment they need. Early mental health support can help a child before problems interfere with other developmental needs.</p>
<p>Myth: People with mental health problems are violent and unpredictable.</p>
<p><strong>Fact:</strong> The vast majority of people with mental health problems are no more likely to be violent than anyone else. Most people with mental illness are not violent and only 3%–5% of violent acts can be attributed to individuals living with a serious mental illness. In fact, people with severe mental illnesses are over 10 times more likely to be victims of violent crime than the general population. You probably know someone with a mental health problem and don't even realize it, because many people with mental health problems are highly active and productive members of our communities.</p>
<p>Myth: People with mental health needs, even those who are managing their mental illness, cannot tolerate the stress of holding down a job.</p>
<p><strong>Fact:</strong> People with mental health problems are just as productive as other employees. Employers who hire people with mental health problems report good attendance and punctuality as well as motivation, good work, and job tenure on par with or greater than other employees.</p>
<p>When employees with mental health problems receive effective treatment, it can result in:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lower total medical costs</li>
<li>Increased productivity</li>
<li>Lower absenteeism</li>
<li>Decreased disability costs</li>
</ul>
<p>Myth: Personality weakness or character flaws cause mental health problems. People with mental health problems can snap out of it if they try hard enough.</p>
<p><strong>Fact:</strong> Mental health problems have nothing to do with being lazy or weak and many people need help to get better. Many factors contribute to mental health problems, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Biological factors, such as genes, physical illness, injury, or brain chemistry</li>
<li>Life experiences, such as trauma or a history of abuse</li>
<li>Family history of mental health problems</li>
</ul>
<p>People with mental health problems can get better and many recover completely.</p>
<p>Myth: There is no hope for people with mental health problems. Once a friend or family member develops mental health problems, he or she will never recover.</p>
<p><strong>Fact:</strong> Studies show that people with mental health problems get better and many recover completely. Recovery refers to the process in which people are able to live, work, learn, and participate fully in their communities. There are more treatments, services, and community support systems than ever before, and they work.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Myth: Therapy and self-help are a waste of time. Why bother when you can just take a pill?</p>
<p>Fact: Treatment for mental health problems varies depending on the individual and could include medication, therapy, or both. Many individuals work with a support system during the healing and recovery process.</p>
<p>Myth: I can't do anything for a person with a mental health problem.</p>
<p>Fact: Friends and loved ones can make a big difference. In 2020, only 20% of adults received any mental health treatment in the past year, which included 10% who received counseling or therapy from a professional. Friends and family can be important influences to help someone get the treatment and services they need by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Reaching out and letting them know you are available to help</li>
<li>Helping them access mental health services</li>
<li>Learning and sharing the facts about mental health, especially if you hear something that isn't true</li>
<li>Treating them with respect, just as you would anyone else</li>
<li>Refusing to define them by their diagnosis or using labels such as "crazy", instead use person-first language</li>
</ul>
<p>Myth: Prevention doesn't work. It is impossible to prevent mental illnesses.</p>
<p>Fact: Prevention of mental, emotional, and behavioral disorders focuses on addressing known risk factors such as exposure to trauma that can affect the chances that children, youth, and young adults will develop mental health problems. Promoting the social-emotional well-being of children and youth leads to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Higher overall productivity</li>
<li>Better educational outcomes</li>
<li>Lower crime rates</li>
<li>Stronger economies</li>
<li>Lower health care costs</li>
<li>Improved quality of life</li>
<li>Increased lifespan</li>
<li>Improved family life</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-0-community-mobilization-and-awareness-raising">5.0 COMMUNITY MOBILIZATION AND AWARENESS RAISING:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-0-community-mobilization-and-awareness-raising" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Community mobilization is a way of engaging community members in all sectors of the community to promote individuals, families, and community actions and to identify community priorities, resources, needs and solutions to promoting good representation participation, good governance, accountability and peaceful changes. It involves bringing together stake holders to raise community awareness of the needs and demands for problem solving and delivery of resources, services and utilization. Strengthen community participation for sustainability and self reliance. It may involve door to door outreach, public meetings participatory activities.</p>
<p>It also involves on going and meaningful widespread participation to ensure involvement of key stakeholders with focus on the poor and the vulnerable groups including the mentally ill persons</p>
<ul>
<li>Steps to community awareness</li>
<li>Determine the level of awareness of the community</li>
<li>Design the awareness program based on responses from the community on their awareness levels.</li>
<li>Have people or groups of people who will take correct messages to the community about what needs to be done in the community</li>
<li>Find ways to become part and parcel of the community</li>
<li>Show the community how much you value them</li>
</ul>
<p>It does this by raising awareness</p>
<ul>
<li>Empowering individuals</li>
<li>Empowering groups</li>
<li>Creating enabling environment</li>
<li>Sensitizing community on positive changes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="importance-of-community-mobilization">Importance of community mobilization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#importance-of-community-mobilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It empowers the community to identify and address their own needs and generating local solutions to problems</li>
<li>Strengthen the ability of communities to work together towards a common goal</li>
<li>Participation of community members in achievement of common goals</li>
<li>It leads to sustainability of any given action</li>
</ul>

<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>○ Help in development of adequate intervention
○ Develop trust in activities
○ Encouraging participation of all community members, the youth, families, communities, and many young groups.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="detecting-mental-health-conditions">DETECTING MENTAL HEALTH CONDITIONS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#detecting-mental-health-conditions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Physical examination: your doctor will try to rule out physical problems that could cause your symptoms.</li>
<li>Lab tests: These may include, for example, a check of your thyroid function or a screening for alcohol and drugs</li>
<li>A psychological evaluation: A doctor or mental health professionals talks to you about your symptoms, thoughts, feeling and behavior patterns. You may be asked to fill out a questionnaire to help answer these questions.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supporting-peole-with-long-term-mental-conditions">SUPPORTING PEOLE WITH LONG-TERM MENTAL CONDITIONS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supporting-peole-with-long-term-mental-conditions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Spiritual support.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stigma-and-discrimination-and-abuse-of-people-with-mental-illness">STIGMA AND DISCRIMINATION AND ABUSE OF PEOPLE WITH MENTAL ILLNESS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stigma-and-discrimination-and-abuse-of-people-with-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Stigma is when someone sees you in a negative way because of your mental illness. Discrimination is when someone treats you in a negative way because of your mental illness.</p>
<p>Social stigma and discrimination can make mental health problems worse and stop a person from getting the help they need.</p>
<p>Avoid stigmatizing people with mental illness by seeing the person first and not labelling them with their mental illness.</p>
<p>You can help challenge stigma by speaking up when you hear people around you make negative or wrong comments about mental illness.</p>
<p>Stigma is when someone sees you in a negative way because of a particular characteristic or attribute (such as skin colour, cultural background, a disability or a mental illness). When someone treats you in a negative way because of your mental illness, this is discrimination.</p>
<p>Stigma happens when a person defines someone by their illness rather than who they are as an individual. For example, they might be labelled' psychotic' rather than 'a person experiencing psychosis'.</p>
<p>For people with mental health issues, the social stigma and discrimination they experience can make their problems worse, making it harder to recover. It may cause the person to avoid getting the help they need because of the fear of being stigmatized.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-harmful-effects-of-stigma">THE HARMFUL EFFECTS OF STIGMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-harmful-effects-of-stigma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Some of the effects of stigma include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Feeling of shame, hopelessness and isolation</li>
<li>Reluctance to ask for help or to get treatment</li>
<li>Lack of understanding by family, friend or others</li>
<li>Fewer opportunities for employment or social interaction</li>
<li>Bullying, physical violence or harassment</li>
<li>Self-doubt-the belief that you will never overcome your illness or be able to achieve what you want in life.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dealing-with-stigma">DEALING WITH STIGMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dealing-with-stigma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Here are some ways you can deal with stigma:</p>
<p><strong>Get the mental health treatment you need.</strong> Try not to let the fear of being labelled with a mental illness stop you from getting help.</p>
<p><strong>Do not believe it.</strong> Sometimes if you hear or experience something often enough, you start to believe it yourself. Try not to let other people’s ignorance influence the way you feel about yourself. Mental illness is not a sign of weakness and is rarely something you can deal with on your own. Talking about your mental health issues with healthcare professionals will help you on your road to recovery or management.</p>
<p><strong>Do not hide away:</strong> many people with mental illness want to isolate themselves from the world. Reaching out to people you trust- family, friends, coaches, or religious leaders-can mean you get the support you need.</p>
<p><strong>Connect with others.</strong> Joining a mental health support group –either online or in person-can help you deal with the feelings of isolation and make you realize that you are not alone in your feelings and experiences.</p>
<p><strong>You are not your illness.</strong> Do not define yourself by your illness as other people might. Instead of saying ‘I’m schizophrenic’, say I have schizophrenia. There is power in language.</p>
<p><strong>It’s not personal.</strong> Remember that other peoples’ judgments often come from a lack of understanding rather than anything else. The judgments are made before they get to know you, so do not believe that their views have anything to do with you personally.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="promotion-and-prevention-of-mental-illness">PROMOTION AND PREVENTION OF MENTAL ILLNESS.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#promotion-and-prevention-of-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Promotion is an approach aimed at strengthening positive aspects of mental health and psychosocial wellbeing, and is focused on empowering people to live healthy lives (e.g. by facilitating healthy lifestyles through policies, such as providing nutritious foods in school canteens or opportunities for physical exercise in accessible locations), rather than health being the sole domain of health professionals (National Research Council and Institute of Medicine, 2009). It includes – for example – components to foster pro-social behaviour, self-esteem, coping, decision-making capacity, but also universal interventions such as social and economic interventions to improve people's social determinants of health which would</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>impact on their wellbeing. Prevention is an approach aimed at reducing the likelihood of future disorder in the general population or for people who are identified as being at risk of a disorder (Eaton, 2012; Tol et al., 2015). Prevention is further subdivided on the basis of the population targeted, into universal, selective and indicated (National Research Council and Institute of Medicine, 2009). Universal prevention, which includes strategies that can be offered to the whole population including individuals who are not at risk, based on the evidence that it is likely to provide some benefit to all (reduce the probability of disorder), clearly outweighs the costs and risks of negative consequences. Examples of common universal prevention interventions include the community-wide provision of information on positive coping methods (IASC, 2007) to help people feeling safe and hopeful, protection against human rights violations (e.g. gender-based violence), community-wide efforts to improve livelihoods as a key protective factor for mental health.</p>
<p>Selective prevention refers to strategies that are targeted to subpopulations identified as being at elevated biological, social or psychological risk for a disorder but who are asymptomatic or have very minimal symptoms. These interventions involve human, supportive and practical help covering both a social and a psychological dimension. They work through communication (asking about people needs and concerns; listening to people and helping them to feel calm), practical support (i.e. providing meals or water) and with a psychological approach including teaching stress management skills and helping people to cope with problems (World Health Organization, 2011); facilitation of community support for vulnerable individuals by activating social networks and communication; structured cultural and recreational activities supporting the development of resilience (National Research Council and Institute of Medicine, 2009), such as traditional dancing, art work, sports and puppetry. These activities may take place in equipped settings with the aim of increasing the children's sense of connectivity and safety (Tol et al., 2011).</p>
<p>Indicated prevention includes strategies that are targeted to individuals who are identified (or individually screened) as having detectable signs or symptoms which can foreshadow, precede and may sometimes – if left unaddressed – lead to a full diagnosable mental disorder based on an individual assessment. These interventions to prevent mental disorders may be delivered at individual or group level, in a variety of settings (antenatal and postnatal visits, home visits, community settings, schools, etc.). These interventions include psychosocial support for persons with subclinical levels of mental disorders (Purgato et al., 2019a), such as</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  t u d o c u</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>mentoring programmes aimed at children with behavioural problems; psychological first aid for people with heightened levels of psychological distress after exposure to severe stressors, loss or bereavement (Tol et al., 2015). This includes facilitator-guided self-help group interventions, as for example the WHO Self-Help Plus (Epping-Jordan et al., 2016; Purgato et al., 2019a).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adult-mental-health">ADULT MENTAL HEALTH.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adult-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mental health problems and neurological disorders among older adults account for approximately 10 to 15 % of the total disability of the world elderly group 60 years and above</p>
<p>Older adults have higher chances of developing mental health problems due to substance abuse, diabetes, and other health conditions. As the world population increases does the number of the old with mental health conditions.</p>
<p>The most common mental and neurological disorders in the old are dementia, depression, anxiety, substance abuse. This conditions cases almost a half of the elderly deaths and self-harm.</p>
<p>It is important to consider the effect of mental health disorders in the elderly because this condition is always ignored, misdiagnosed and overlooked in this age group. Also the stigma surrounding the condition makes people reluctant to seek help</p>
<p>Risk factors to mental health among the elderly</p>
<ul>
<li>Life stressors</li>
<li>Losses of capacity</li>
<li>Decline in functional ability</li>
<li>Reduced mobility</li>
<li>Chronic pains</li>
<li>Life experiences like bereavement</li>
<li>Drop in social economic status</li>
<li>Isolation</li>
<li>Loneliness</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Psychological depression</li>
</ul>
<p>Older people are as well vulnerable to elderly abuse such as physical abuse, verbal abuse, psychological, financial, sexual, abandonment, neglect, loss of dignity and respect. These life experiences may lead the elderly to developing physical injury, psychological problems, depression and anxiety.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is important to prepare health providers with training and knowledge on management of age-related chronic diseases including mental neurological and substance abuse disorders</p>
<p>Development of suitable policies on long term and palliative care. development of age friendly services</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-promotion">Health promotion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-promotion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This involves the following activities</p>
<ul>
<li>Promoting healthy aging</li>
<li>Creating healthy conditions</li>
<li>Creating environment that supports wellbeing of the elderly</li>
<li>Provision of resources to meet the elderly needs</li>
<li>Providing security and freedom good housing</li>
<li>Social support</li>
<li>Health and social programs</li>
<li>Deal with elderly abuse</li>
<li>Prompt recognition and treatment of mental disorders</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: currently there is no known cure for dementia but much can be done to support and improve the lives of those with the condition which includes</p>
<p>Early diagnosis to promote early management</p>
<ul>
<li>Identify and treatment underlying conditions</li>
<li>Detecting and managing challenging conditions</li>
<li>Providing information and long term support to care.</li>
</ul>

<p>Good general health and social care is important for promoting older people’s health, preventing disease and managing chronic illnesses. Training all providers in working with issues and disorders related to ageing is therefore important. effective community level primary mental health care for older is important</p>
<p>Supportive legislative environment based on accepted human rights standards is required to ensure the rights and highest quality of services to people with mental illness and their caregivers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="child-mental-health">CHILD MENTAL HEALTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#child-mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mental health in children means reaching developmental and emotional milestones and learning healthy social skills and how to cope when there is problem</p>
<p>Mental health in children means positive quality of life and function at home, in school, and in the community</p>
<p>Mental disorder in children means changes in the ways children typically learn, behave or handle their emotions which causes stress and problem getting through the day.</p>
<p>Mental health in children is important to the overall health. mental disorder are chronic health conditions that last a long time and often don't go away completely without early diagnosis and treatment children with mental disorders can have problems at home, in schools and in forming friends and can continue to adulthood. Many children have fear and worries and may feel sad and hopeless from time to time. strong fear may appear at different times during development. persistent or extreme form of fear and sadness could be due to either anxiety or depression</p>
<p>Some common childhood mental disorder includes</p>
<ul>
<li>Attention disorder</li>
<li>Anxiety disorder- fears</li>
<li>Depression – being sad</li>
<li>Behavior disorder</li>
<li>Learning and developmental disability</li>
<li>Autism</li>
<li>Substance use</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Symptoms of mental health disorder in children may start in early childhood or develop in teenage. most diagnosis is done during school age but some may pass without being diagnosed. Some symptoms may include the following,</p>
<ul>
<li>Difficulties with plays</li>
<li>Difficulties in learning</li>
<li>Difficulties in speaking</li>
<li>Difficulties in controlling emotions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<ul>
<li>Talk to the child</li>
<li>Notice how the child behave at home, in school and with friends</li>
<li>Notice how the child is able to control ether anger worries or sadness.</li>
<li>Early diagnosis and treatment is equally important</li>
<li>Teachers should identify children with problems and work with families and health professional to help children with mental health problems</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="integration-of-people-with-mental-health-disorder-in-communities">Integration of people with mental health disorder in communities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#integration-of-people-with-mental-health-disorder-in-communities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Discrimination and abuse of persons with mental illness, children with mental health and developmental problems.</p>
<p>It is illegal for discrimination of the mentally ill in all situations including, work place, rejection, promotion, forced activity, denying job</p>
<p>If an individual is able to show that the impact of his mental condition may lead to disability and he is treated unfairly because of that condition then it illegal to do so. Mental health may lead to disability that is protected under the Equality Act. 2010. Some included are sex, age, race.</p>
